                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">عَادِ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, indecl., with kesr for its termination, is a particle in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ</foreign>, governing an accus. case, on the condition of its being preceded by a verbal proposition and a conjunction; as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">رَقَدْتُ وَعَادِ أَبَاكَ سَاهِرٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I slept, and verily thy father was waking,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">remaining awake, by night</hi>]:          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  it is also an interrogative particle in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">هَلْ</foreign>, indecl., with kesr for its termination, requiring an answer; as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">عَادِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَبُوكَ مُقِيمٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Is thy father abiding?</hi>]:          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  it also denotes an answer, in the sense of a proposition rendered negative by means of <foreign lang="ar">لم</foreign> or of <foreign lang="ar">ما</foreign>, only; indecl., with kesr for its termination; and this is when it is conjoined with a pronoun; as when <pb n="2190"/> an interrogator says, <foreign lang="ar">هَلْ صَلَّيْتَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Didst thou perform,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hast thou performed, the act of prayer?</hi>], and thou answerest, <foreign lang="ar">عَادِنِنى</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Verily I</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">إِنَّنِى</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">did not perform,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">have not performed, the act of prayer:</hi>          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  and some of the people of El-Hijáz suppress the <foreign lang="ar">ن</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">عَادِنِى</foreign>: both the modes are chaste when <foreign lang="ar">عَادِ</foreign> is used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ</foreign>:          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  sometimes, also, it is used by the interrogator and the answerer; the former saying, <foreign lang="ar">عَادِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَ زَيْدٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Did Zeyd go forth?</hi> or <hi rend="ital">has Zeyd gone forth?</hi>], and the latter saying, <foreign lang="ar">عَادِهِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Verily he did not go forth,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">has not gone forth:</hi>          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  all this is unmentioned by the leading authors on the Arabic language, those of lengthy compositions as well as the epitomisers.
